    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer85663857785700212">Macon Leary is a travel writer who hates both travel and anything out of the ordinary. He is grounded by loneliness and an unwillingness to compromise his creature comforts when he meets Muriel, a deliciously peculiar dog-obedience trainer who up-ends Macon’s insular world and thrusts him headlong into a remarkable engagement with life.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7299527" />
    <a title="Ellen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/240603-ellen"><img alt="Ellen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1212021041p2/240603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/7299527?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellen" href="/user/show/240603-ellen">Ellen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer7299527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer696302329055583859">It looks like I'm in the minority here, but I really did not enjoy this book. I couldn't sympathize with any of the characters. I thought Macon was whiny and indecisive. I couldn't be compelled to care about what he wanted, mostly because it was never made clear to me exactly what that was. He just seemed to bump along with whatever happened. <br/><br/>More than anything else, my problem with this book is that nothing happened. I kept thinking that possibly in the next chapter Macon would act in some way </span>
  <span id="freeText696302329055583859" style="display:none">It looks like I'm in the minority here, but I really did not enjoy this book. I couldn't sympathize with any of the characters. I thought Macon was whiny and indecisive. I couldn't be compelled to care about what he wanted, mostly because it was never made clear to me exactly what that was. He just seemed to bump along with whatever happened. <br /><br />More than anything else, my problem with this book is that nothing happened. I kept thinking that possibly in the next chapter Macon would act in some way to change his own destiny, but nope. Nothing even happened in the end, the book just seemed to stop. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1772322107" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1772322107" />
    <a title="Michael Finocchiaro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48483884-michael-finocchiaro"><img alt="Michael Finocchiaro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576692048p2/48483884.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1772322107?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Finocchiaro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Finocchiaro" href="/user/show/48483884-michael-finocchiaro">Michael Finocchiaro</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=novels">novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=american-20th-c">american-20th-c</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48483884-michael-finocchiaro?shelf=pulitzer-fiction">pulitzer-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1772322107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10523645417883245209">I adored this book! Appreciated it more than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31181.Breathing_Lessons' title='Breathing Lessons by Anne Tyler' rel='nofollow noopener'>Breathing Lessons</a> or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77699.Dinner_at_the_Homesick_Restaurant' title='Dinner at the Homesick Restaurant by Anne Tyler' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dinner at the Homesick Restaurant</a>. It is touching and hilarious and timeless.<br/><br/>Macon lives alone with his misbehaving dog Edward in the wake of the double catastrophe of his son Ethan being murdered while away at summer camp and his wife Brenda walking out on him. He is not in great shape: <b>He felt much worse in the morning. It had been a warm night and he woke up sticky and cross. He couldn't face the thought of popcorn for breakfas</b></span>
  <span id="freeText10523645417883245209" style="display:none">I adored this book! Appreciated it more than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31181.Breathing_Lessons" title="Breathing Lessons by Anne Tyler" rel="nofollow noopener">Breathing Lessons</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77699.Dinner_at_the_Homesick_Restaurant" title="Dinner at the Homesick Restaurant by Anne Tyler" rel="nofollow noopener">Dinner at the Homesick Restaurant</a>. It is touching and hilarious and timeless.<br /><br />Macon lives alone with his misbehaving dog Edward in the wake of the double catastrophe of his son Ethan being murdered while away at summer camp and his wife Brenda walking out on him. He is not in great shape: <b>He felt much worse in the morning. It had been a warm night and he woke up sticky and cross. He couldn't face the thought of popcorn for breakfast. He laundered a load of sheets and then, in the midst of hanging them, found himself standing motionless with his head bowed, both wrists dangling over the clothesline as if he himself had been pinned there.</b> (p. 57) This particular scene reminded me of the one in Don Quixote when he is standing on poor Rocinante's back looking spying through a window at his beloved Dulcinella, but Rocinante sees a piece of grass lying on the ground and wanders over to it leaving Quixote suspended in space, mike Macon. Wonderful image!<br /><br />He moves in with his equally maladjusted brothers Charles and Porter and his sister Rose to fight the feeling of loneliness, but this still looks to him like a poor solution: <b>Charles and porter on either side of him, Rose perched in the foreground. Was there any real change? He felt a jolt of something very close to panic. Here he still was! The same as ever! <i>What have I gone and done?</i> he wondered, and he swallowed thickly and looked at his own empty hands.</b> (p. 81)<br /><br />Macon is the author of the popular travel guides <u>The Accidental Tourist</u> which are tourists books for businessmen that travel for work, helped along by his friend and boss Julien. Before leaving on a trip, he is rebuffed by a kennel who will not take Edward for him because he bit someone on a previous stay. This mishap leads us to the other protagonist, the wonderfully ebulent and verbose Muriel who, over at the Meow-Bow animal hospital, takes in Edward and offers to train him: <br /><b>"I can even teach split personality."<br />"What's split personality?"<br />"Where your dog is, like, nice to you but kills all others."<br /> "You know, I think I may be in over my head here," Macon said.</b> (p. 97) This is typical of the quirky and direct talking style of Muriel and a small sample of the rich humor throughout the book or the small observations such as when Edward seems to be learning too quickly in Muriel's presence: <b>the way a toothache will improve the moment you step into a dentist's waiting room.</b> (p. 101) See also the training session on p. 114. So funny!<br /><br />Macon and his siblings are all in a sort of suspended animation, stuck in their thoughts and in their ways. Muriel represents an escape from this monotony which Macon embraces, rejects and ultimately embraces - this tension and back and forth forming the backbone for this excellent book. His transformation is not without pain and risk, however: <b>He was gone too far to return. He would never, ever get back. He had somehow traveled to a point completely isolated from everyone else in the universe, and nothing was real but his own angular hand clenched around the sherry glass.</b> (p. 180)<br /><br />This is truly a wonderful novel, full of love and humor and I truly preferred it over the other two Tyler books I have read so far. A fantastic read and it still surprises me that she missed the Pulitzer. One of my next reads is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/256008.Lonesome_Dove" title="Lonesome Dove by Larry McMurtry" rel="nofollow noopener">Lonesome Dove</a> which won out over this one...</span>
  <a data-text-id="10523645417883245209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_968309823" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/968309823" />
    <a title="Joe Valdez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez"><img alt="Joe Valdez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585885999p2/26876584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/968309823?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe Valdez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe Valdez" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez">Joe Valdez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780394546896" href="/book/show/77695.The_Accidental_Tourist">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26876584-joe-valdez?shelf=fiction-general">fiction-general</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer968309823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12927871054556570131">Love is in the air--or maybe anxiously repressed--in February and my romantic literature jag concludes with <i>The Accidental Tourist</i>, the 1985 novel by Anne Tyler and winner of the National Book Critics Circle Award for Fiction that year. Like all of my reads in the shortest month of the year, this was my introduction to the author and I found much of Tyler's story to be an absolute delight. This is a novel by and for mature adults that finds a wonderful balance between the melancholy of losing a </span>
  <span id="freeText12927871054556570131" style="display:none">Love is in the air--or maybe anxiously repressed--in February and my romantic literature jag concludes with <i>The Accidental Tourist</i>, the 1985 novel by Anne Tyler and winner of the National Book Critics Circle Award for Fiction that year. Like all of my reads in the shortest month of the year, this was my introduction to the author and I found much of Tyler's story to be an absolute delight. This is a novel by and for mature adults that finds a wonderful balance between the melancholy of losing a child and long term spouse in the same year and the excitement of meeting someone new, with its awkwardness, miscommunication and urges to flee to the familiar.<br><br>The story focuses on Macon Leary, a methodical and steady man of 42 who's introduced driving himself and his mercurial wife Sarah home from a beach vacation that wrapped up early when neither found the heart for it. His wife sports a suntan. Macon does not. His determination to keep driving through a heavy rainstorm despite Sarah's apprehension escalates into her declaration that she can't live with him anymore and wants to move out. Their house in an older part of Baltimore is left to Macon to occupy alone with Edward, a Welsh corgi which belonged to the couple's only child Ethan, murdered at the age of 12 along with the other diners in a fast food restaurant.<br><br>Macon is a reluctant travel writer, author of a series of guidebooks called <i>The Accidental Tourist</i> catering to businessmen and others forced into foreign locales when they'd prefer the comforts of home. Twelve years ago, Macon was sort of helping run a bottle-cap factory inherited with his brothers Charles and Porter from their grandfather. Macon's interest in writing and working for a newspaper led to an article in a local weekly on a crafts fair. The article was all about Macon's fussiness at the fair but caught the attention of Julian Edge, publisher of Businessman's Press, who identified a niche and offered Macon a job.<br><br><i>It was one of Macon's bad habits to start itching to go home too early. No matter how short a stay he'd planned, partway through he would decide that he ought to leave, that he'd allowed himself far too much time, that everything truly necessary had already been accomplished--or almost everything, almost accomplished. Then the rest of the visit was spent in phone calls to travel agents and fruitless trips to airline offices and standby waits that came to nothing, so that he was forced to return to the hotel he'd just checked out of. He always promised himself this wouldn't happen again, but somehow it always did. In England, it happened on his fourth afternoon. What more was there to do? he started wondering. Hadn't he got the gist of the place?</i><br><br>Neither Macon or his dog Edward take it well when Sarah moves out and their sorry state contributes to Macon slipping down the basement stairs and breaking his leg. To recuperate, Macon moves back home to be taken care of by his sister Rose, a fixer who also cares for his gifted but socially challenged brothers Charles and Porter, as well as the neighborhood's elderly. Edward terrorizes the household to the point where the siblings read Macon the riot act. For help, he turns to Muriel Pritchett, an animal caretaker he left Edward with at the Meow-Bow Animal Hospital before his trip to England. <br><br>Nothing about Muriel--from her frizzy hair to her eclectic fashion sense to her youth--appeals to Macon, who has never dated anyone except his stately wife Sarah and has little interest in starting. He ignores Muriel's overtures to meet for a drink or to let her cook him dinner, despite observing a cockiness that impresses him. Muriel works wonders with Edward, but when Macon learns from a co-worker that she has a seven-year-old son, he attempts to cancel their dinner date, terrified of emotional involvement. Muriel gets Macon to open up about his late son and in comforting him, the relationship blossoms. <br><br>Macon begins spending time at Muriel's home in an impoverished section of Baltimore, sleeping over, cleaning up and even writing there. He takes an interest in her frail boy Alexander, whose allergies Macon believes have been exaggerated by the boy's mother. Muriel exposes him to her crazy quilt of relationships. Dominick is a teenager who handles her car repairs in exchange for the keys three nights a week. Her 17 year old sister Claire has ongoing drama with their disapproving mother and sleeps over regularly. Macon struggles to find consistency in Muriel's behavior, while admiring her courage as well.<br><br><i>Had he ever known such a fighter? He went grocery shopping with her unusually late one evening, and just as they were crossing a shadowed area a boy stepped forth from a doorway. "Give over all what you have in your purse," he told Muriel. Macon was caught off guard; the boy was hardly more than a child. He froze, hugging the sack of groceries. But Muriel said, "The hell I will!" and swung her purse around by its strap and clipped the boy in the jaw. He lifted a hand to his face. "You get on home this instant or you'll be sorry you were ever born," Muriel told him. He slunk away, looking back at her with a puzzled expression.<br><br>When Macon had caught his breath again, he told Muriel she was a fool. "He might have had a gun, for all you knew," he said. "Anything might have happened! Kids show less mercy than grown-ups; you can see that any day in the papers."<br><br>"Well, it turned out fine, didn't it?" Muriel asked. "What are you so mad at?"<br><br>He wasn't sure. He supposed he might be mad at himself. He had done nothing to protect her, nothing strong or chivalrous. He hadn't thought as fast as she had or thought at all, in fact. While Muriel ... why, Muriel hadn't even seemed surprised. She might have strolled down that street expecting a neighbor here, a stray dog there, a holdup just beyond--all equally part of life. He felt awed by her, and diminished. Muriel just walked on, humming "Great Speckled Bird" as if nothing particular had happened.</i><br><br>Macon reluctantly invites Muriel to his sister Rose's wedding to his publisher Julian, who believes he's found in the Learys the old-fashioned domestic comfort that he's always craved. Macon will not so much as commit to bringing Muriel to visit Paris with him or give in to her desire for a June wedding. His family continue to her refer to his girlfriend as "that Muriel person." The final push Macon needs to flee a new commitment comes when his wife Sarah concedes she's ready to come home, that at a certain age, people just don't have much of a choice and that it's too late for her to change her life. <br><br>For much of <i>The Accidental Tourist</i>, I wanted to shrink Anne Tyler and put her in my pocket. I was struck by how effortlessly she mixed tragedy and comedy into a narrative that I found mirrored certain aspects of my own life so accurately. The horror of losing a child in the violent and senseless manner which Macon and Sarah do is something I hope I never experience but Tyler slips into the story in a way that is both powerful and restrained. I could relate to Macon's social anxiety and that of his family's to dip their toes into the unfamiliar and how a woman who never seems to think further ahead than a minute challenges him to do just that.<br><br>Muriel's behavior did overstep boundaries that today would evoke a restraining order, but I was okay with experiencing it in a novel from a far less sensitive time. Tyler's prose is adroit, her dialogue a delight and story absent of caricature, with the stiffness of a WASP male relaxed by the vitality of a woman who's had to fight for everything in her life. The simple joys of the book made for strange bedfellows with a big movie, which was well reviewed and nominated for four Academy Awards in 1988 but barely memorable today. Adapted by Frank Galati and Lawrence Kasdan and directed by Kasdan, it featured William Hurt as Macon, Geena Davis as Muriel, Kathleen Turner as Sarah and Bill Pullman as Julian.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488152784i/22085206._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12927871054556570131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_170601599" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170601599" />
    <a title="Fabian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1036893-fabian"><img alt="Fabian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514061293p2/1036893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170601599?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fabian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fabian" href="/user/show/1036893-fabian">Fabian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170601599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15841918862820831511">Accidental tourists are pretty annoying! (These are those pesky travelers who refuse to give up all their customs, their comforts; refuse to get lost a little in the foreignness, to LIVE.) And this book isn't. A success then! (considering the subject matter.) Yeah, the protagonist is a huge bore & as he has one of the best jobs of all time is doubly douche-ey, but he has a reason to be maudlin and dissatisfied. Lifetime Movie Network viewers would have a blast... & the novel feels capital D Date</span>
  <span id="freeText15841918862820831511" style="display:none">Accidental tourists are pretty annoying! (These are those pesky travelers who refuse to give up all their customs, their comforts; refuse to get lost a little in the foreignness, to LIVE.) And this book isn't. A success then! (considering the subject matter.) Yeah, the protagonist is a huge bore &amp; as he has one of the best jobs of all time is doubly douche-ey, but he has a reason to be maudlin and dissatisfied. Lifetime Movie Network viewers would have a blast... &amp; the novel feels capital D Dated indeed. But Tyler does a great job in making all characters believable and all situations credible... you feel very bad for the guy you basically would hate to have around you. His intellectual edge is minuscule, and you feel bad for all other "dumber" characters too. It's slightly symbolic, but also rather, um, small.<br /><br />It is wise to note that other books by this particular publishing company such as "The Patron Saint of Liars" by Anne Patchett or "The World According to Garp" by John Irvin also seem to fit within this category of above-average reads-- which you may or may not be inspired to recommend, depending on the mood, the weather or the person.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15841918862820831511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Anne Bogel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7494963-anne-bogel"><img alt="Anne Bogel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560950142p2/7494963.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1821911255?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne Bogel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne Bogel" href="/user/show/7494963-anne-bogel">Anne Bogel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1821911255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12044360593274124202">I've been meaning to read Anne Tyler for years, and when podcast guest Rebecca Smith (Jane Austen's 5x great niece) said she thought Tyler should be recommended reading for Jane Austen fans, I finally took the plunge. This was an enjoyable read that wasn't anything like I expected, and was relatable in surprising ways. Now I want to read more Anne Tyler, of course. (The question is: which one?)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_64050373" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64050373" />
    <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely"><img alt="K.D. Absolutely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471967140p2/2156200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64050373?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K.D. Absolutely" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely">K.D. Absolutely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to K.D. by: </span>
      501 Must Read Books (Modern Fiction)
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=family-drama">family-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=501">501</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=pulitzer">pulitzer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=tragicomic">tragicomic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=1001-core">1001-core</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer64050373&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64050373" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12816402981958742540">“Burying one’s child is against the flow of nature,” said the wife of the Speaker of the House (Philippine Congress) in her eulogy for her 16-year old daughter several years ago. Her only daughter got burned when their short-circuited Christmas tree went in flames. The clueless poor daughter was sleeping and got trapped inside her room. No one was with here in the house when that happened.<br/><br/>This is one thought that, whenever it crosses my mind, I always whisk away immediately: <i>the death of my chil</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12816402981958742540" style="display:none">“Burying one’s child is against the flow of nature,” said the wife of the Speaker of the House (Philippine Congress) in her eulogy for her 16-year old daughter several years ago. Her only daughter got burned when their short-circuited Christmas tree went in flames. The clueless poor daughter was sleeping and got trapped inside her room. No one was with here in the house when that happened.<br /><br />This is one thought that, whenever it crosses my mind, I always whisk away immediately: <i>the death of my child.</i> Typing it here even feels wrong as I remember reading that mind has that power to attract what you always think of. I just don't know what to do if this happens. I might as well kill myself, I guess. However, this thing happens. It’s one of the sad realities of life. Once we are born, we can die <i>anytime</i>. In fact, I have some friends and acquaintances whose children died ahead of them. <br /><br />I also read and liked books that have this as its main or underlying theme. <i>Ordinary People</i> (1976) by Judith Guest was my first. The older son (Buck) died while sailing with the younger son (Conrad) and the unspoken guilt of the son and the unexpressed emotion of the parents blaming the younger son who survived was so powerful that when it was made into a movie, it won the Academy Awards for Best Picture. That was in 1980.<br /><br />Second, was a book that I read a couple of years back and topped my list of my favorites for that year: <i>What I Loved</i> (2003) by Siri Husvedt. The grief is also not as openly expressed as in Ordinary People but the child who died was their only one and there was no one to blame as the death was an accident. Similarly, the devastated couple separated and the father tried to see his dead child from same-age children of his friends or even strangers. In this book, <i>The Accidental Tourist</i>, the father, <b>Macon Leary</b> starts to withdraw to his own world <i>he would imagine that his whole body was enclosed in a cast and people would peep into the hole in his eyes and would asked “Macon, are you there?”</i> However, Tyler's story went further: Macon seems to belief that the soul of his dead son, <b>Ethan</b> remains in his son’s dog, <b>Edward</b> and no matter how strange or brutal the dog behaves, he keeps it and even hires a dog-trainer <b>Muriel</b> to tame the dog.<br /><br /><i>The Accidental Tourist</i> was the 1985 novel by Anne Tyler (born 1941). A finalist at Pulitzer Prize and won the National Book Critics Award Circle for Fiction. the novel was adapted into a 1988 award-winning film starring William Hurt (as Macon Leary), Kathleen Turner (Sarah, his estranged wife) and Geena Davis (Muriel, the dog trainer). Davis won the Best Actress in a Supporting Role in this film for the succeeding year’s Academy Awards. <br /><br />This is my first Anne Tyler novel. Her writing is straightforward. No-frills yet incandescently clear. It’s an easy read. You’ll have a feeling that you are watching a movie (although I missed this film but I will not forego a chance of seeing it). Her strength seemingly is her strong way of building her characters. She goes inside their minds and she seems to have the ability to know how the character should behave in the circumstances that they are in. Her women characters are not stereotyped: they can be as brutal as <b>Sandra</b> leaving Macon to his solitude, as funny yet decisive as <b>Muriel</b> who fights for her love and her son Alexander or as eccentric but loyal, vulnerable yet loving as <b>Rose</b> who arranges her groceries in alphabetical order and cries over the fact that her brothers would not want to eat her cooked-overnight-in-low-fire turkey. Then there are the Leary brothers: Macon (the father), Charles and Porter and they all are poor in direction that they always get lost even if they are just going to the corner store. This book is peppered with many memorable characters that I had a feeling that I was standing in front of a buffet table and I am confused which one to put on my plate as my favorite.<br /><br />I used to ignore the books of Anne Tyler but next time that I see <i>Dinner at the Homesick Restaurant</i> that Tyler said to be her best work or <i>Breathing Lessons</i> that won the Pulitzer Prize in 1989, I will surely buy them right there and then. Be it bargain or regular-priced. Anne Tyler can surely give back the value of every penny you have in your pocket.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12816402981958742540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Antoinette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5328952-antoinette"><img alt="Antoinette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503842818p2/5328952.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2269305164?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Antoinette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Antoinette" href="/user/show/5328952-antoinette">Antoinette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2269305164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11025578809147717931">I absolutely adored this book. It was the perfect read for right now. When I wasn’t reading it, I was thinking about the people in this book.<br/><br/>Anne Tyler writes people- people you can recognize. They are middle class people who live their lives as best as they can. You can almost sense that she spends her time studying and processing people to get to their inner selves.<br/><br/>The Leary siblings in this book are as straight-laced as they come. Outsiders have trouble relating to them. They are unique and i</span>
  <span id="freeText11025578809147717931" style="display:none">I absolutely adored this book. It was the perfect read for right now. When I wasn’t reading it, I was thinking about the people in this book.<br /><br />Anne Tyler writes people- people you can recognize. They are middle class people who live their lives as best as they can. You can almost sense that she spends her time studying and processing people to get to their inner selves.<br /><br />The Leary siblings in this book are as straight-laced as they come. Outsiders have trouble relating to them. They are unique and idiosyncratic.<br />Macon Leary is a man who has gone through the worst devastation and he is tottering on the edge. He is a man who keeps his thoughts and feeling inside, so he is a hard man to read. Others see him as a cold man, but is he?<br /><br />“It occurred to him (not for the first time) that the world was divided sharply down the middle: Some lived careful lives and some lived careless lives, and everything that happened could be explained by the differences between them.”<br /><br />There were many laugh out loud moments, especially when Edward, the dog, was involved. There were also many tender moments in this book. This book made me laugh and it made me tear up.<br /> <br />This is the second Anne Tyler book I have read (I’m a late bloomer when it comes to Anne Tyler), and I am so excited to know there are many more for me to savour.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11025578809147717931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_167999469" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167999469" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4542979-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454402751p2/4542979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167999469?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/4542979-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140083408" href="/book/show/910576.The_Accidental_Tourist">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=buddy-reads-with-jemidar">buddy-reads-with-jemidar</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167999469" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1534485421464841616">This is a warm, wise, funny, heart-breaking and ultimately life-affirming book. In Macon Leary, the man who writes travel books for people who hate to travel, Tyler has created an amazing character. His damaged psyche, his vulnerability, the gradual changes in his character and outlook as he starts to connect with the messiness of living leap off the page. This book makes me laugh out loud one moment and brings tears to my eyes the next. Although Macon is the centre of the novel, the supporting </span>
  <span id="freeText1534485421464841616" style="display:none">This is a warm, wise, funny, heart-breaking and ultimately life-affirming book. In Macon Leary, the man who writes travel books for people who hate to travel, Tyler has created an amazing character. His damaged psyche, his vulnerability, the gradual changes in his character and outlook as he starts to connect with the messiness of living leap off the page. This book makes me laugh out loud one moment and brings tears to my eyes the next. Although Macon is the centre of the novel, the supporting characters are also wonderful creations. There's Muriel - vulnerable and needy, but alive and connected to others. There's Macon's fabulously eccentric siblings, his boss Julian, his wife Sarah and even his dog Edward - each of them real and memorable. <br /><br />Some fifteen years after last reading what is without doubt my favourite of Anne Tyler's novels, it was a joy to return to it as a buddy read with my friend Jemidar. If anything, I loved the novel even more than I did when I read and loved it all those years ago. I'm quite sure that I'll read it again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1534485421464841616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1527306766" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1527306766" />
    <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen"><img alt="Helene Jeppesen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528006866p2/21992464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1527306766?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helene Jeppesen" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen">Helene Jeppesen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1527306766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10837967278133491869">Yet another simple, but beautiful story from Anne Tyler about Macon whose son died a couple of years ago, and whose wife suddenly decides to leave him. Macon is a middle-aged man, and he has no idea how to continue living on his own. It's remarkable to see what changes he goes through during the 400 pages of this novel, and it's an inspiration to read about him as well as the people he surrounds himself with. <br/>Throughout most of this book, I was thinking to myself: What exactly is it that makes m</span>
  <span id="freeText10837967278133491869" style="display:none">Yet another simple, but beautiful story from Anne Tyler about Macon whose son died a couple of years ago, and whose wife suddenly decides to leave him. Macon is a middle-aged man, and he has no idea how to continue living on his own. It's remarkable to see what changes he goes through during the 400 pages of this novel, and it's an inspiration to read about him as well as the people he surrounds himself with. <br />Throughout most of this book, I was thinking to myself: What exactly is it that makes me like this book so much? It's almost too simple to deserve a 4-star-rating, but after having finished it I believe that it's the underlying messages and themes of life that makes it deserve 4 stars from me. I was comforted when reading this novel because I quickly fell in love with the characters (as well as the less-than-lovely dog Edward). It made me feel good to read about them, and I felt for Macon and all of the changes he went through. <br />Anne Tyler is a remarkable author because she writes simplistic stories that manages to hit you spot-on. "The Accidental Tourist" is just another cast of characters from her that I know will follow me for many days to come. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10837967278133491869" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen Gallup" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen Gallup" href="/user/show/1266077-stephen-gallup">Stephen Gallup</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26131437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8953088035221908851">I’ve read and enjoyed most of Anne Tyler’s novels (starting with <i>Searching for Caleb</i>, which author Don Barthelme recommended to me years ago). A character from one of her first books (I think it was <i>If Morning Ever Comes</i>) provided the name I later gave to my daughter. <i>The Accidental Tourist</i> strikes closest to home with its theme of coping with a profound loss and then the ultimate redemption that comes from such an unexpected direction. It was while reading this book in about 1987 that I first f</span>
  <span id="freeText8953088035221908851" style="display:none">I’ve read and enjoyed most of Anne Tyler’s novels (starting with <i>Searching for Caleb</i>, which author Don Barthelme recommended to me years ago). A character from one of her first books (I think it was <i>If Morning Ever Comes</i>) provided the name I later gave to my daughter. <i>The Accidental Tourist</i> strikes closest to home with its theme of coping with a profound loss and then the ultimate redemption that comes from such an unexpected direction. It was while reading this book in about 1987 that I first felt moved to pick up a pen and begin scratching out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10507622-what-about-the-boy-a-father-s-pledge-to-his-disabled-son" rel="nofollow noopener">my own story</a>.<br /><br />I should say that the book and the movie are forever intertwined in my mind now: When I think of Macon and Muriel, I see William Hurt and Geena Davis. It’s very rare for the film version of any book to be anywhere near as good as the source, but in this case both are excellent. The cameo appearance of the French boy who looks just like Macon’s lost son takes my breath away every time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8953088035221908851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <a title="Barry Pierce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barry Pierce" href="/user/show/4593541-barry-pierce">Barry Pierce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780701129866" href="/book/show/1083372.The_Accidental_Tourist">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593541-barry-pierce?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4593541-barry-pierce?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1426871103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12896646966114513966">Macon Leary writes travel companions under the nom de plume The Accidental Tourist. The irony is that while he helps thousands of people keep their lives together as they travel, he cannot help his own life from falling apart before his eyes.<br/><br/>This is my first Anne Tyler, a writer who I've always relegated to someone that my mother might enjoy. To give context, my mother's reading habits consist of whatever was 3 for 2 in Tesco. However, since many people who I respect have given very positive rev</span>
  <span id="freeText12896646966114513966" style="display:none">Macon Leary writes travel companions under the nom de plume The Accidental Tourist. The irony is that while he helps thousands of people keep their lives together as they travel, he cannot help his own life from falling apart before his eyes.<br /><br />This is my first Anne Tyler, a writer who I've always relegated to someone that my mother might enjoy. To give context, my mother's reading habits consist of whatever was 3 for 2 in Tesco. However, since many people who I respect have given very positive reviews to Tyler in the past I thought I'd give her a go. Sadly, this didn't really do anything for me. I did enjoy the overall plot but the characters, especially Macon, were just <i>such</i> boring people. The type that you'd cross the road for if you saw them walking towards you. I found myself putting this novel down more than I picked it up. Its slice-of-life monotony is usually something that I look for in a novel but <i>The Accidental Tourist</i> just gave me... monotonous monotony. Oh well. I haven't given up all hope though. I'll definitely be visiting Anne Tyler again soon. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12896646966114513966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/360971-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1197938725p2/360971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/221550300?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/360971-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/360971-amy?shelf=didn-t-finish">didn-t-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer221550300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11574264642796824297">Apologies in advance to my book group. I promise to keep my mouth shut and let someone explain to me why they like this book, because I can't figure it out.<br/><br/>The main character, Macon, is so compulsive and deranged. I read reviews of the book where people thought the descriptions of his daily routines were humorous. I found no humor, only desperation and pathos. His life and psychotic narrative going on in his head was too depressing for words. Reading this book made me anxious to get back to my l</span>
  <span id="freeText11574264642796824297" style="display:none">Apologies in advance to my book group. I promise to keep my mouth shut and let someone explain to me why they like this book, because I can't figure it out.<br /><br />The main character, Macon, is so compulsive and deranged. I read reviews of the book where people thought the descriptions of his daily routines were humorous. I found no humor, only desperation and pathos. His life and psychotic narrative going on in his head was too depressing for words. Reading this book made me anxious to get back to my life that I'm happy with and not try and live with such sad characters.<br /><br />Muriel was so pushy and desperate. It was not endearing, it was scary. I know there were some parts in there that were supposed to show that Macon was good for Muriel's son Alexander, but Macon and Muriel's relationship was so dysfunctional, I couldn't bear to watch Alexander tormented by their instability. I skipped ahead to try and see where their relationship was going. Muriel let that man in to her son's life knowing that he was still conflicted about his ex-wife? <br /><br />This book is not a comedy, it's not romantic, it is tragic. And the saddest part is that I imagine that there are so many people who like this story and these characters because they know people who live like this and think these are normal relationships.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11574264642796824297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16507465216617708927" style="display:none">I guess this will always be one of my all time favourite books. For me, it worked on all levels, I loved the story, characters and the routine absurdities that form part and parecel of everyday life. There is tragedy, humour and romance. I think this is the best book Anne Tylor has written and I've read all of them. Nowhere else does she captures the nuances of relationships so well. On a personal level, this book will always mean a lot to me, introducing a kind of anal retentive anti hero who yet manages to be both appealing and desirable. We learn that organisation is a fear of chaos and that sometimes the organised amongst us must venture into the chaotic to fully realise our potential. It also taught me that heroism comes in many shapes and forms and that it is not always the handsome and strong who caspture our hearts.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12447901230390055652"><br/>Buddy read with Kim.<br/><br/>I first read this back in the late eighties and loved it, and recently decided to do a re-read just to see if I still loved it as much. I've changed and my life circumstances have changed, so I wondered... <br/><br/>And I'm happy to say that not only do I still love it, but I think I love it a lot more than I did the first time around.   <span id="freeText12447901230390055652" style="display:none"><br />Buddy read with Kim.<br /><br />I first read this back in the late eighties and loved it, and recently decided to do a re-read just to see if I still loved it as much. I've changed and my life circumstances have changed, so I wondered... <br /><br />And I'm happy to say that not only do I still love it, but I think I love it a lot more than I did the first time around. Call it accumulated life experience if you like, but it had a resonance and a poignancy that touched me at a much deeper level. I laughed, I cried, I cheered Macon on, and hissed when someone threatened to get in the way of his journey out of grief. At times his story was heartbreaking but it was ultimately uplifting, so worth every second I spent in his company. I would love to count Macon Leary amoung my friends.<br /><br />Anne Tyler is an amazing author. She makes her flawed and quirky characters so vulnerable and human, and writes about them so compassionately that you can't help but like them and empathize with them. I don't know of another author who can reach out from the page and make me feel so deeply or care so much. She is a real talent.<br /><br />I would highly recommend this book to all :-).<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1658316104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13050984153581324381">This is the first “classic” Tyler I’ve read, after her three most recent novels, and although I kept being plagued by odd feelings of ‘reverse déjà vu’, I really enjoyed it. This story of staid, reluctant traveler Macon Leary and how his life is turned upside down by a flighty dog trainer is all about the patterns of behavior we get stuck in. Tyler suggests that occasionally journeying into someone else’s unpredictable life might change ours for the good.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer99756258308727944">On the way home from a trip, Sarah tells Macon that she wants a separation. They lost their son a year ago and both have been just going through the motions of life. What follows is a devastating, humorous, uplifting and satisfying series of events and adventures that begin when Macon agrees to have his wayward Corgi Edward trained by Muriel, a strange but enthusiastic employee he meets at the Meow Bow Animal Hospital.<br/><br/>I just fell in love with these characters and their quirks. I loved how the au</span>
  <span id="freeText99756258308727944" style="display:none">On the way home from a trip, Sarah tells Macon that she wants a separation. They lost their son a year ago and both have been just going through the motions of life. What follows is a devastating, humorous, uplifting and satisfying series of events and adventures that begin when Macon agrees to have his wayward Corgi Edward trained by Muriel, a strange but enthusiastic employee he meets at the Meow Bow Animal Hospital.<br /><br />I just fell in love with these characters and their quirks. I loved how the author fit together the most unlikely pairs and showed how they brought out the best in each other. I didn't always agree with the decisions that they made, but nothing felt contrived or forced. The ending was quite a shock and I'm not sure what the future holds for these characters and their choices, but it was a good place for the author to end the book. <br /><br />Recommended for those that enjoy a character driven book without a focused plot or concrete ending.</span>

<div id="review_2621431334" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2621431334" />
    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2621431334?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/40041238-the-accidental-tourist">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2621431334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16552096172939573679">Macon Leary is infuriatingly by the book. He writes guidebooks for business travelers so they can avoid any unexpected roadblocks or disturbances. Everything in his life has an order, until a shooting at a burger joint takes the life of his twelve year old son. This disrupts his marriage and life as he knows it, with his wife Sarah ultimately leaving him. When he encounters Muriel, a dog trainer who works at his dog's kennel, he learns to embrace the new and exciting things in life. <br/><br/>As always, A</span>
  <span id="freeText16552096172939573679" style="display:none">Macon Leary is infuriatingly by the book. He writes guidebooks for business travelers so they can avoid any unexpected roadblocks or disturbances. Everything in his life has an order, until a shooting at a burger joint takes the life of his twelve year old son. This disrupts his marriage and life as he knows it, with his wife Sarah ultimately leaving him. When he encounters Muriel, a dog trainer who works at his dog's kennel, he learns to embrace the new and exciting things in life. <br /><br />As always, Anne Tyler is a master at observation. Her characters are so quirky and full of life, but not too exaggerated to be unrealistic. She has little nuggets of wisdom sprinkled throughout that fit so naturally into the story, and when you come across one you can't help but be deeply moved. I loved Macon's development throughout the story and enjoyed learning about his upbringing, how that shaped his present, and to see him move his life towards a new future. Tyler is a master at storytelling and character-building, and holds her claim as one of my all-time favorite authors.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16552096172939573679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_26528750" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26528750" />
    <a title="Maureen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/680205-maureen"><img alt="Maureen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1232569180p2/680205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26528750?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maureen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maureen" href="/user/show/680205-maureen">Maureen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer26528750&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26528750" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8824077155362779615">This book was so interesting to me. I thoroughly enjoyed the characters, especially the Leary family (they over intellectualize everything, correct grammar, and have major OCD and I felt like I could relate to them so well). Ann Tyler has a unique style of writing a novel, which left me always wanting to know more. Everything she wants to say is there...but it may be hidden in symbolism, in conversations, in small actions. It reads almost like a play, in stage directions (Macon chooses a tie) an</span>
  <span id="freeText8824077155362779615" style="display:none">This book was so interesting to me. I thoroughly enjoyed the characters, especially the Leary family (they over intellectualize everything, correct grammar, and have major OCD and I felt like I could relate to them so well). Ann Tyler has a unique style of writing a novel, which left me always wanting to know more. Everything she wants to say is there...but it may be hidden in symbolism, in conversations, in small actions. It reads almost like a play, in stage directions (Macon chooses a tie) and conversation. You have to read a little between the lines to catch the wealth of story that Tyler is offering.<br /><br />I found myself very pleased with the end of the novel, which surprised me. I like Ann Tyler's way of sneaking up on you through an interesting story and then revealing to you at the end that what you believed were absolutes are actually gray areas (Barbara Kingsolver does this to me too). <br /><br />From my standpoint, the (morally) right thing, the thing Macon should have done, was to try to stay with his wife. But, they weren't a good match, they no longer had children together, Muriel was so much better for him...and so I felt like he made the right choice, despite all I personally believe(d?) to the contrary. Which left me feeling...uncomfortable. Because more black and whites have just been proven grays after all...<br /><br />But I realized that the book is not about deciding to leave a marriage or make it work. Macon and Sarah's marriage is really meant to illustrate people (like Macon) who lead "accidental" lives, who never "take steps." Tyler shows us that people who are trapped in their grooves, like the entire Leary clan, can "take steps" and can change and let new things and new experiences into their lives. Macon is a man who has always done things the same way, because it has been a way that has worked for him. After his son's death, however, it no longer became an adequate method for coping with life. To me this story is so hopeful and happy because Macon does find a new way of life and he realizes that there is not one right way to live, there can be many, and that is what makes life so full.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8824077155362779615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2288335087" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2288335087" />
    <a title="Dawnie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36293066-dawnie"><img alt="Dawnie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464172620p2/36293066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2288335087?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dawnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dawnie" href="/user/show/36293066-dawnie">Dawnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783596108220" href="/book/show/2298696.Die_Reisen_des_Mr_Leary">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36293066-dawnie?shelf=paperbacks">paperbacks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36293066-dawnie?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36293066-dawnie?shelf=german-books">german-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2288335087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15775448486004628034">So far this is defiantly my least favourite of Tyler's books. <br/><br/>Surprisingly so, since at the beginning i really enjoyed how... lets call it specific the main character is. <br/><br/>I love that we clearly have this character that loves order, routines and everything exactly as he wants it for no other reason other than that it makes him feel better to have it that way. <br/><br/>And of course its Tyler's fantastic writing. <br/><br/>But the actual plot, the other characters and even the main character started to go on my nerv</span>
  <span id="freeText15775448486004628034" style="display:none">So far this is defiantly my least favourite of Tyler's books. <br /><br />Surprisingly so, since at the beginning i really enjoyed how... lets call it specific the main character is. <br /><br />I love that we clearly have this character that loves order, routines and everything exactly as he wants it for no other reason other than that it makes him feel better to have it that way. <br /><br />And of course its Tyler's fantastic writing. <br /><br />But the actual plot, the other characters and even the main character started to go on my nerves half way through the book. <br /><br />And i am not even sure why. <br /><br />Its a good story. <br /><br />Loosing a child, having your partner leave you shortly after than and having to cope with all of that is hard. So of course if you rite about a character that goes through those things, he will go through a good amount of changes throughout the entire book. And it wasn't that it bothered me how Macon changed. <br /><br />It was everything else around him. <br /><br />I thought that all characters were either overly extreme in their behaviour or completely under developed and not at all what i am used to with Tyler's other books and characters. <br />In some way all characters in this book where whinny in some way or other. <br /><br />They where unhappy, so that could be excused with that BUT for the most part non of the characters seemed to want to change their whinny and frankly pount-y feeling behaviour. <br /><br />There are some changes with the characters throughout the book, but in my option they just became even worse instead of better. <br /><br />Maybe it is the wrong time for me to read this. <br /><br />I don't seem to have the right mind set right no to read literary fiction, especially this type where I kind of just want to scream and the characters to just deal with their issues and get on with it because what the heck?? There are bigger problems in life and what the heck are they doing?<br />I mean even with this book and the talk about losing a child in such a way as its described in this book... <br /><br />I felt like the characters and story itself focused on all the wrong things. <br /><br />I am sure i will re-read this in the future. <br /><br />And i hope i will enjoy it more than, since it seems to be one of the rather loved books by Tyler. <br /><br />But for right now i am disappointed and feeling a bit like i want to shake the book to see if that makes it better. As stupid as that might sound.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15775448486004628034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1865167620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1865167620" />
    <a title="Nita Kohli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/808367-nita-kohli"><img alt="Nita Kohli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482664517p2/808367.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1865167620?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nita Kohli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nita Kohli" href="/user/show/808367-nita-kohli">Nita Kohli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780143012405" href="/book/show/1083363.The_Accidental_Tourist">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1865167620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2964167379774530383">When I began reading this book, I was not sure if I will really like it. But, then it was a book from Anne Tyler so I continued on because she is one of the authors I am a big fan of. She is my go to author when I dont know what to read or when I am feeling low and I find her books feel-good-books. <br/>Thank God that my faith in Anne Tyler made me not give up this book early on because I simply loved this book. This book was, to put it simply, beautiful. I just loved it...wait did I say that already</span>
  <span id="freeText2964167379774530383" style="display:none">When I began reading this book, I was not sure if I will really like it. But, then it was a book from Anne Tyler so I continued on because she is one of the authors I am a big fan of. She is my go to author when I dont know what to read or when I am feeling low and I find her books feel-good-books. <br />Thank God that my faith in Anne Tyler made me not give up this book early on because I simply loved this book. This book was, to put it simply, beautiful. I just loved it...wait did I say that already?<br />The book has such a bunch of crazy characters and I still ended up loving them all. I even liked the dog, Edward! Macon is one character whom I loved, felt sorry for and also hated at some point of time. There were times when I vouched for Muriel and disliked Sarah. But, in the end I felt that you cannot really take sides in a story like this. It is extremely difficult and I can truly understand Macon's dilemma and struggles.<br /><br />In all, another amazing book from Anne Tyler. I have so many books from this author lined up on my shelf and I continue to hoard her books.<br /><br />Leaving you with my favorite quotes from this book. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It is not how much you love someone, but who you are when you are with him.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote></span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/91482850?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/3301814-james">James</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3301814-james?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91482850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18446013024929196381">I am an unabashed Ann Tyler fanboy. She can write about things that in another author`s hands would be mundane or cliched but with her remain completely riveting, warm and funny and desperately sad. The Accidental Tourist is the story of a man with very limited ability to handle change who in the aftermath of his sons death tries to live. This may not sound like the funniest scenario ever but there are some great moments. Loved it.</span>
  <span id="freeText18446013024929196381" style="display:none">I am an unabashed Ann Tyler fanboy. She can write about things that in another author`s hands would be mundane or cliched but with her remain completely riveting, warm and funny and desperately sad. The Accidental Tourist is the story of a man with very limited ability to handle change who in the aftermath of his sons death tries to live. This may not sound like the funniest scenario ever but there are some great moments. Loved it.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1425242340" />
    <a title="Kiwi Begs2Differ  ✎" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12287031-kiwi-begs2differ"><img alt="Kiwi Begs2Differ  ✎" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556698979p2/12287031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1425242340?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiwi Begs2Differ  ✎" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiwi Begs2Differ  ✎" href="/user/show/12287031-kiwi-begs2differ">Kiwi Begs2Differ  ✎</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12287031-kiwi-begs2differ?shelf=gen-fiction-contemp">gen-fiction-contemp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12287031-kiwi-begs2differ?shelf=z_2015-monthly-genre">z_2015-monthly-genre</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1425242340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2506220657510291128">I have mixed feelings about this book. I enjoyed the tenderness and melancholy of the writing. I struggled often with the very slow pace of the story that deals with the lonely and monotonous life of a middle-aged man grieving over a failed marriage and the loss of his only child. For me the strength of the book are the characters, which are delicately drawn, and their relationship with each other. 2 ½ stars. </span>

          </span>
        </div>
